  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_de688d7d-5a63-4749-87fd-b280788fb487'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText8732538412048091450" style="display:none">A vast improvement over the last two installments in the 39 Clues series, "Storm Warning" finally reveals the mystery behind both the Madrigals and what Nellie Gomez has been up to since the clue hunt began. <br /><br />This time, Dan and Amy Cahill are off to the Caribbean, searching for clues about the pirate Anne Bonny and other historical figures of the area. "Storm Warning" has a good pace and none of the clue hunting seems to rushed as it was in the two previous books in the series. I loved learning more about Nellie, as well as seeing Natalie Kabra getting some more pagetime as well. <br /><br />I'm still a little worried how they're going to wrap everything up in one more book, but the ending to "Storm Warning" explains all of that pretty clearly. All-in-all, a great book to rev up excitement for the last book in the series! </span>

Things are finally coming together and being revealed as Dan and Amy race around the world - this time in the Caribbean - against relatives on the hunt for the 39 clues.   <span id="freeText16897136217216877773" style="display:none">4.5 stars. One of the best books in this series yet! Things are finally coming together and being revealed as Dan and Amy race around the world - this time in the Caribbean - against relatives on the hunt for the 39 clues. The narration's viewpoint shifted between a few of the characters, so we got to see how others were feeling, and there was excitement mixed with danger and red herrings. The author was one of the better writers, too, which made the reading super quick and smooth. The reveal at the end was clever and made sense of much of the plot of the series so far, so I'm eager to see how the next book ties it all up!</span>

  <span id="freeText15609782949765512553" style="display:none">This was the best 39 clues book I have ever read and that is saying something.<br />That's why it deserves the 5 stars I gave it, though I really mean to give it 4.5 stars.<br />I did not expect this book to be so good, I did not expect to get so engrossed in it ,or feel so much excitement over it. <span id="freeTextContainer8391457202906097650">I'm going to give a generic review of the series. Basically because I'm lazy and don't want to write 39 reviews. Okay, 11.<br/><br/>We finally read Book 1. And then because we liked it so well, the entire series. One son (age 12) has read them all, the second son (also age 12) is on Book 2.   <span id="freeText8391457202906097650" style="display:none">I'm going to give a generic review of the series. Basically because I'm lazy and don't want to write 39 reviews. Okay, 11.<br /><br />We finally read Book 1. And then because we liked it so well, the entire series. One son (age 12) has read them all, the second son (also age 12) is on Book 2. And son #3 (age 8) will be starting as soon as he finishes his current book.<br /><br />I thought the premise of this book very interesting. I loved how they integrated history and geography along with problem-solving skills and code cracking. Add in the action, humor and intrigue and kids (and some adults) can't put them down. All three of us that have read 39 Clues thought Book 2 the weakest of the series. But as one son said, after finishing the series, "Gordon Korman seems to be getting better. I think he's a decent author now." <br /><br />Some of the books are better at teaching the history part, others just barely skim the surface and you don't really learn about the person they're 'highlighting'. I appreciate that they're clean books - no curse words or you-know-what going on. There is some violence (very little, if any, blood) and several murder attempts, but they never work.<br /><br />The series would most likely be called twaddle by my Charlotte Mason friends. I do, however, think it has more redeeming qualities than most kids literature and I'm happy to see my boys devouring a book every day or so.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12290262777727625364" style="display:none">Dan and Amy want to find the next clue to their clue hunt, but some people are getting in the way of things like the man in the black suit, Natalie and Ian, and possibly Nellie too. So, Dan and Amy try to keep their secrets (clues) to themselves, and with help from Nellie, Dan and Amy get to the places they needed to go like the Caribbean. This story is about trust and loyalty. This was one of my favorite books to read the series, it had me gripping my sheets when I stayed up to read it in bed, and I am sure you will have the same reaction too.</span>

<div id="review_98691533" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98691533" />
    <a title="Kristin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85084-kristin"><img alt="Kristin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440089749p2/85084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98691533?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin" href="/user/show/85084-kristin">Kristin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98691533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16198954430650787361">This was one of the better books in this series...maybe I'll read more by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/61707.Linda_Sue_Park' title='Linda Sue Park' rel='nofollow noopener'>Linda Sue Park</a>. But anyway, this book explains many things that I had questions about before. Without giving too much away, I can't say much more. However, I'm starting to have serious doubts on whether they will be able to put a solid, worthy ending on this series in just one more book. There is just so much going on...and I'm hoping that Book 10 is a good, final piece like with Harry Potter. If it's anti-climatic, I'm go</span>
  <span id="freeText16198954430650787361" style="display:none">This was one of the better books in this series...maybe I'll read more by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/61707.Linda_Sue_Park" title="Linda Sue Park" rel="nofollow noopener">Linda Sue Park</a>. But anyway, this book explains many things that I had questions about before. Without giving too much away, I can't say much more. However, I'm starting to have serious doubts on whether they will be able to put a solid, worthy ending on this series in just one more book. There is just so much going on...and I'm hoping that Book 10 is a good, final piece like with Harry Potter. If it's anti-climatic, I'm going to be highly disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16198954430650787361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_200577093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200577093" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5483155-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350755658p2/5483155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200577093?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/5483155-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5483155-jenn?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5483155-jenn?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5483155-jenn?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5483155-jenn?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200577093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8111711527100395476">***NOTE MY REVIEWS OFTEN CONTAIN SPOILERS***<br/><br/>After the events in China, the Cahill siblings feel they have no choice but to confront Nellie, because they’re sure Nellie isn’t what she claims to be and they need to know exactly what kind of enemy might be among them. Even though they were expecting it, it still blows them away when Nellie confesses to be working for Mr. McIntyre. Along the search for the clue Nellie has become the only family they had and now she’s confessed that they can’t trust </span>
  <span id="freeText8111711527100395476" style="display:none">***NOTE MY REVIEWS OFTEN CONTAIN SPOILERS***<br /><br />After the events in China, the Cahill siblings feel they have no choice but to confront Nellie, because they’re sure Nellie isn’t what she claims to be and they need to know exactly what kind of enemy might be among them. Even though they were expecting it, it still blows them away when Nellie confesses to be working for Mr. McIntyre. Along the search for the clue Nellie has become the only family they had and now she’s confessed that they can’t trust her and she’s been sharing their secrets all along. Feeling betrayed and heartbroken, the trio journey to the Bahamas and Jamaica, following the trail of Anne Bonny, the pirate from the locket. But with Isabel Kambra hard on their heels there isn’t time for heart break if they intend to survive. With no one but each other to trust, will Amy and Dan survive the islands?<br /><br />Like with my previous few reviews, I wrote one review and posted a rating on goodreads after first reading it, but alas that original review was in a notebook that grew legs and ran away. So I reread the book for the purpose of review and I’m sticking with the original rating because I believe books are bast rated after first reading. That and regardless of the fact I like to write reviews I don’t like rating books So I’m not putting myself through making that decision twice. <br /><br />As with all the books in this series, the story presents a wealth of information in the form of a thrilling adventure. This one however shares history on a topic no child could resist – pirates! Following the clue hunt is more than just an adventure for readers, it’s a lesson in history and geography that will hopefully inspire young readers to search for more information on the topics they’re given a taste of in this tale. What’s wonderful about how the information is presented here though is that children don’t even realize they’re learning as they read about Amy and Dan’s adventures in the search for the 39 Clues. The book is a well written close third person with multiple view points and fast pacing. Though filled with information, danger and adventure, this book actually focuses more on the characters. We learn about the clue hunt, but we also learn about how the lives of the Cahills and even their au pair have been maneuvered practically since birth to prepare them for the clue hunt they currently face. Learning this gives all of them a sense of disillusionment added to their au pair’s betrayal it opens us up to more of Amy and Dan’s sensitivities. The characters become even more real as they don’t come across as just adventurers here, they come across as children whose whole world has been torn apart by these events. One thing I didn’t like is that in some ways the characters weren’t as true to form as they’d been in the other novels, Dan’s always been the computer geek while Amy’s into books. Dan’s kind of the hands on puzzles kind of guy while Amy’s the book smart serious worry wort. Or at least that’s how it’s been in the other novels. In this book there’s a scene where Dan correct Amy’s terminology and Amy’s downloading stuff on the computer. Amy’s making up crazy words and Dan’s worrying more than normal. I mean they weren’t completely out of character but it just seemed sort of switched around. The book is filled with action and answers we’ve been searching for throughout the clue hunt are finally revealed which is awesome, but with all the characters introspectiveness and the way they choose at one point to attack rather than defend it’s a little different from other books in the series. Usually Amy and Dan don’t seek out their Cahill relatives, they run from them, in this novel they turn the tables which is unusual but it also goes along with what they’re learning about the historical figures presented in this book. Though each character undergoes a lot of introspection, it doesn’t slow down the plot in anyway because there’s more than enough danger, action and adventure to keep the pace moving along quickly. <br /><br />Like I said above though it has a lot of everything else, the focus of this book is the characters and it includes a lot of introspective moments which allow us to better know the characters and those characters to grow. Amy and Dan have their quirky moments which I mentioned about but are otherwise true to form and gain a new depth in this novel when faced with their au pairs betrayal and how to deal with that. Nellie is torn between her alliances to the children and to her employer. She’s on the outside and she doesn’t know how to get back in and there’s a big part of her that doesn’t care about the job anymore, just the kids. We see her character really grow in this novel as she sees how the Cahill children weren’t the only ones molded for the clue hunt, she was as well. She reflects on how Grace affected her life and how she in turn has affected Amy and Dan’s. Another thing I really enjoyed was seeing into Natalie Kambra. Natalie hasn’t had a lot of spotlight in the previous novels and we start to understand why she is like she is, and how she rationalizes her behavior. She’s starting to question her mother’s action and then berate herself for doing so and there’s a lot of internal struggle going on for this character. I think for the first time ever Natalie actually becomes a little girl as a character rather than just another villain. She’s finally human and that’s kind of impressive.<br /><br />Overall this was an excellent addition to the 39 Clues Series and like always I recommend to readers young and old and am excited to get to the next title.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8111711527100395476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_883571483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/883571483" />
    <a title="Juan Pantoja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24057167-juan-pantoja"><img alt="Juan Pantoja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379649171p2/24057167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/883571483?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juan Pantoja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juan Pantoja" href="/user/show/24057167-juan-pantoja">Juan Pantoja</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer883571483&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer883571483" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9806855958886000956">This book is the first in the 39 clues series to reveal lots of information of the madrigals history. It also reveals the name and identity of the man in black. The genre is Mystery.<br/><br/>The setting is the Beijing Airport, Bahamas, and lastly Jamaica. Amy and Dan want to go to The Bahamas to learn about a pirate named Anne Bonny, dressed as a man in the 1700s because it would lead them to the next clues. When Amy and Dan got their they went to the Oceanus to have some fun and then search for clues. L</span>
  <span id="freeText9806855958886000956" style="display:none">This book is the first in the 39 clues series to reveal lots of information of the madrigals history. It also reveals the name and identity of the man in black. The genre is Mystery.<br /><br />The setting is the Beijing Airport, Bahamas, and lastly Jamaica. Amy and Dan want to go to The Bahamas to learn about a pirate named Anne Bonny, dressed as a man in the 1700s because it would lead them to the next clues. When Amy and Dan got their they went to the Oceanus to have some fun and then search for clues. Later, they wanted to go to a cave in an island near The Bahamas because they heard that famous pirates went their to hide treasure, and they could of left clues their. But when they entered the cave, a big wave came and the cave was flooding so they got out and barely made it out alive. They managed to find a shark tooth that had something to do with the clue hunt. Later they went to Jamaica, Kingston so they can find more about Anne Bonny and the shark fang they just found. They found someone called miss Alice who knew a lot about the fang and Anne Bonny. Miss Alice let them stay in there house because she knew them and because Grace talked to her about them. Ever since they stayed with her, they have been learning so much about the Cahill's history. You'll have to read the book to learn about the madrigal history and the man in blacks name and who's side he's on. The conflict is person vs. person and person vs. nature because a hurricane and storm, and quick sand almost killed both of them and their friends.(Someone dies of drowning in the book). Amy is the sister of Dan and she is the oldest. Miss Alice is a friend of Grace.<br /><br />I think this book is number 2 in the best books I've read because of all the information and close deaths that where written so well so we can understand it if multiple things are happening in the story. These book is related to the 39 clues book 8 because that's where a lot about Amy and Dan were revealed, and it also revealed that Amy and Dan where madrigals.<br /><br />Another reason it's a good book is that it talks about places that I never knew about and what goes on and what the weather is like in those country's, because Amy and Dan travel a lot for clues. This book is related to my life because as time goes on I reveal what I want to do for a living and also like traveling like Amy and Dan do.<br /><br />Overall I think this is a really good book for people that want to learn about the world and what weather can do. I would also recommend it to people that want to know more about Amy and Dan's branch. I would rate it 9.5/10 because it has a really we'll story but the vocabulary that's hard to say. This book will make you understand the rest of the story really well.</span>

<div id="review_313295144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313295144" />
    <a title="Tony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7170903-tony"><img alt="Tony" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313295144?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tony" href="/user/show/7170903-tony">Tony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313295144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1406448811889136128">Storm Warning by Linda Sue Park is another good book that I have read in a series. I have not reviewed the whole series because I read all the others last year. Continuing their quest for all 39 Clues, Amy and Dan travel to the Caribbean to uncover the secrets of Anne Bonny, a famous lady pirate, and a Cahill, the most powerful family in the world. Almost all great people are actually Cahills, but a tragedy broke the family into four branches: The Tomas, masters of physical prowess and the most </span>
  <span id="freeText1406448811889136128" style="display:none">Storm Warning by Linda Sue Park is another good book that I have read in a series. I have not reviewed the whole series because I read all the others last year. Continuing their quest for all 39 Clues, Amy and Dan travel to the Caribbean to uncover the secrets of Anne Bonny, a famous lady pirate, and a Cahill, the most powerful family in the world. Almost all great people are actually Cahills, but a tragedy broke the family into four branches: The Tomas, masters of physical prowess and the most athletic clan, The Ekaterina, the intelligent and wise clan, made up of brilliant inventors and thinkers, The Janus, the most artistic and creative branch, most comprised of artists and musicians, and The Lucian, the ruthless strategists, dictators and businesspeople. There is actually a secret fifth branch which all other ones fear: The Madrigal. Founded after the other branches, this mysterious branch's mission is actually to stop the Clue Hunt and join the warring clans back together. Amy and Dan know that all thirty nine clues will make them become the most powerful people in the world, but are doing it for their dead parents and grandma, to finish what they started. With other clans hot on their tail, this series is all about action. I really like how their is almost action in every chapter, and the series is very fast paced and unpredictable. It is also one of the most creative ideas for a book. Each book in the series is unique, because each book is written by a different author. The only problem with this one was, I just didn't get the 39 Clues feel in it. Even though a friend dies, I don't really feel the personal value in the characters. <br /><br />Dan and Amy arrive in the Caribbean and discover various items that help them locate the clue. The one thing they do differently this time is instead of being the prey, they become the predator. They lure the Kabras, a deadly Lucian family, into a trap and recover a key trinket which aids them in the Clue Hunt. Sadly, tragedy strikes and one of their allies die in the conflict with the Kabras. Once they open the box with the trinket, they finally discover the clue of the region and their mysterious enemy's identity. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1406448811889136128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_226368667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226368667" />
    <a title="05chrise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6168360-05chrise"><img alt="05chrise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314742657p2/6168360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226368667?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="05chrise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="05chrise" href="/user/show/6168360-05chrise">05chrise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226368667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2303651755415984264">Storm Warning, by Linda Sue Park<br/><br/>	This ninth addition to the 39 clue book series is actually kind of confusing at the beginning because you can’t tell what it is leading up to. Amy and Dan Cahill have been all over the world on their clue hunt to become the most influential people in the history of the world, but the Caribbean is by far the nicest place they have been in yet! But is not even close to the safest place they have been, either. They are being followed by the man in black, a mysteriou</span>
  <span id="freeText2303651755415984264" style="display:none">Storm Warning, by Linda Sue Park<br /><br />	This ninth addition to the 39 clue book series is actually kind of confusing at the beginning because you can’t tell what it is leading up to. Amy and Dan Cahill have been all over the world on their clue hunt to become the most influential people in the history of the world, but the Caribbean is by far the nicest place they have been in yet! But is not even close to the safest place they have been, either. They are being followed by the man in black, a mysterious man that has tried to kill them multiple times. But one thing is certain: he is a Madrigal, just like Dan, Amy, and their parents! They also have enemies ready to kill them at a moment’s notice with henchmen at their disposal. Concussions, quicksand, water parks, and lots of other unexpected things add to the intensity of the book, with all sorts of un-thought-of twists in the plot, leading to an uncertain end!<br /><br />	 This book is yet another action-packed book full of surprises that are unlike what you are used to the characters being like. It is good at attacking your emotions, making you sad by the characters moods or revengeful for what you know other characters have done to the main characters. One such example is excellent to prove this statement completely! “I was right there with him- and then a wave- and he’s stuck in the quicksand- we’ve got to save him,” said Dan through tears. This is when a character is lost and could be drowning, which is why the sentence is told so spastically.<br /><br />	This book was not all amazing, and was kind of crazy because of all the twists and curves in the story that makes you kind of angry at the writer for doing those parts so strange. Also, when the main characters help save their enemy’s lives, and in return, they are left in a situation that will probably kill them! It was just kind of disturbing to think that some people actually think like that! I recommend this book to anyone who loves to read and even those whose attention span is short, because it will hook you right from the start!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2303651755415984264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_262226384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262226384" />
    <a title="Irene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6382707-irene"><img alt="Irene" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262226384?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene" href="/user/show/6382707-irene">Irene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6382707-irene?shelf=february">february</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262226384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6256389943580821296"> Storm Warning is the continuation of the book, The Emperor's Code. This series is about two siblings, Amy and Dan. You might think they are just average people, but the truth is that their family, the Cahills, is on a hunt all around the world looking for 39 clues that can change the world. In the book Storm Warning, Dan and Amy starts of their next clue search in Bahamas, hoping to find more information about a pirate who they believe is a Cahill, thinking that she (the pirate was a girl) was </span>
  <span id="freeText6256389943580821296" style="display:none"> Storm Warning is the continuation of the book, The Emperor's Code. This series is about two siblings, Amy and Dan. You might think they are just average people, but the truth is that their family, the Cahills, is on a hunt all around the world looking for 39 clues that can change the world. In the book Storm Warning, Dan and Amy starts of their next clue search in Bahamas, hoping to find more information about a pirate who they believe is a Cahill, thinking that she (the pirate was a girl) was the one who hid the clue. They start searching, little did they know that they were being watched by Isabella and her two children, who are also on the search for clues and the man in black. After finding the first piece of the clue, Dan and Amy make their way to Jamaica. There, they face more obsticles and encounter Isabella and the others. As they come closer to finding the next clue, the man in black appears, but why? <br /><br /> I picked this book up because I didn't want to stop at the eighth book. I wanted to know what would happen to Dan and Amy and the whole Cahills family. I read this book's summary and thought that it would be intresting since Dan and Amy will finally find out who was the man in black.<br /><br /> I finished this book because they didn't reveal who the man in black was until the very end. Also, I wanted to know why Nellie was working/helping the man in black, I always thought that she was on Amy and Dan's side. There were many other things I wanted to find out, that's why I finished this book.<br /><br /> I would recommend this book to anyone who likes the 39 Clues series. In my opinon, this book was probably the most intresting out of all nine of the books I read in this series. I can't wait to read the 10th one! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81069549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81069549?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81069549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3483150913386107303">Reviewed by Jennifer Rummel for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Amy and Dan have become quite suspicious of their au pair, Nellie. While traveling to the Caribbean for the next part of the hunt, they force Nellie into telling them the truth about her secret conversations. As much as it pains Nellie, she only tells them part of it. She's been working for Mr. McIntyre because Grace hired her. Grace wanted to be sure Amy and Dan could take part in the hunt, as they needed a chaperon. All this time, Nellie's been r</span>
  <span id="freeText3483150913386107303" style="display:none">Reviewed by Jennifer Rummel for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Amy and Dan have become quite suspicious of their au pair, Nellie. While traveling to the Caribbean for the next part of the hunt, they force Nellie into telling them the truth about her secret conversations. As much as it pains Nellie, she only tells them part of it. She's been working for Mr. McIntyre because Grace hired her. Grace wanted to be sure Amy and Dan could take part in the hunt, as they needed a chaperon. All this time, Nellie's been reporting back to Mr. McIntyre.<br /><br />Amy and Dan can't believe what they're hearing. How could they have trusted her? Now, they realize that they can't trust anybody, except themselves.<br /><br />While in Jamaica, they find a significant piece of a clue. With a little bit of research, they uncover knowledge of pirates with Cahill loot. Directly after their research find, Nellie's forced to visit a woman who wants to speak with her. Nellie and her charges are in for a shock. Grace influenced her life in ways she never imagined - more than just hand-picking her as Amy and Dan's au pair.<br /><br />With this new knowledge, will Amy and Dan trust Nellie again? They're running out of people to trust, and as they get closer to the truth behind the 39 clues, the danger keeps escalating. Without her help, they might end up dead, but would trusting her be more dangerous?<br /><br />I love this series. These are quick, engaging reads that I devour. I can't wait for the next book to see how this series ends; it's been an amazing ride. I love all the action, the danger, the many double-crossings, and watching the sibling relationship unfold.</span>

<div id="review_112761648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112761648" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1735763-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442495481p2/1735763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112761648?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1735763-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112761648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17326052971068738596">Having read all the books in this series so far, I am now most anxious to read the final book that is due to come out in August. Every book has captured my attention and Book 9: Storm Warning is no exception. It is aptly titled and if you are an astute observer some things are revealed even before you read the book. That’s one of the things I love about The 39 Clues.<br/><br/><br/>This time 14 year-old Amy Cahill and her 11-year-old brother Dan are in Jamaica, following the lead of Anne Bonny, a pirate of the </span>
  <span id="freeText17326052971068738596" style="display:none">Having read all the books in this series so far, I am now most anxious to read the final book that is due to come out in August. Every book has captured my attention and Book 9: Storm Warning is no exception. It is aptly titled and if you are an astute observer some things are revealed even before you read the book. That’s one of the things I love about The 39 Clues.<br /><br /><br />This time 14 year-old Amy Cahill and her 11-year-old brother Dan are in Jamaica, following the lead of Anne Bonny, a pirate of the 1700s. They meet Lester and his grandmother Alice who play a vital role in helping them find their next clue. Things heat up when, once again, they confront their au pair, Nellie Gomez who reveals that she wasn’t a random college student hired by Aunt Beatrice to be their au pair. She continues to explain in part what her role is vis-à-vis them, her charges. This leaves Dan and especially Amy hurt, angry and very distrustful of her.<br /><br />Suspense builds as the man in black who has followed them closely throughout the hunt, and whom they fear since he tried to kill them in the past, is now very close on their heels. When a tragedy occurs, devastating Dan and Amy, I was initially surprised this would be included in the story. But as the story races to its finish, I understood this plot element perfectly. The Cahill duo are challenged in a test that determines their fate and semi-prepares them for the final confrontation with the man in black and their superior role in the clue for the 39 clues. Another satisfying and cliffhanger ending. Can’t wait to read the next and final book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17326052971068738596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+h+idZll/JWk6x+tjrcB8gAOjKSrQYiApND+NRajh/z7StI0L3LhSXEPnvgGVxE7Q0uJk++cv2nucpOQUD6RXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17944698074807688679">Linda Sue Park is a Korean American author of children's fiction. Park published her first novel, Seesaw Girl, in 1999. To date, she has written six children’s novels and five picture books for younger readers. Park’s work achieved prominence when she received the prestigious 2002 Newbery Medal for her novel A Single Shard.<br/><br/></span>
